+Jamison Brereton

12 (632)
Indra
Parvata K─Бс╣Зva
33 verses: uс╣гс╣Зih, arranged in trcas. ╠е
R╠еgveda VIII.12 is tightly structured: the meter is uс╣гс╣Зih (8 8 12), and in each tr╠еca the last four syllables of the final p─Бda form a refrain, which is, however, syntacti cally integrated into the verse. The last two tr╠еcas before the final one (vss. 25тАУ27, 28тАУ30) expand the four-syllable refrain to full p─Бda length (that is, the final twelve syllables), which retards the verbal progress and hints at the end to come. The long refrain of verses 25тАУ27, тАЬjust after that your two beloved fallow bays waxed strong,тАЭ echoes the short refrain of the second tr╠еca (vss. 4тАУ6), тАЬyou have waxed strong,тАЭ and thus hints at a ring composition as well.
The verb form shared by those two refrains (тАЬwaxed strong,тАЭ root vakс╣г) is found elsewhere in the hymn, as are synonyms (root vr╠еdh: тАЬgrow strong, make strong, increaseтАЭ) and near synonyms (тАЬspread,тАЭ тАЬswellтАЭ), and this verbal material pro vides the thematic spine of the hymn. Otherwise there is a mixture of mythological material, especially toward the end, and invitations to and descriptions of the sac rifice. In the final tr╠еca (vss. 31тАУ33) the poet announces the launch of his own hymn, that is, the hymn to which this tr╠еca forms the end, and asks for the usual bounties from Indra.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWe solicit, most powerful Indra, who are the deep quaffer of the Soma, that exhilaration whichcontemplates (heroic deeds), whereby you slay the devourer (of men).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

We solicit: tam imahe: we solicit you aspossessing that exhilaration, t─Бdс╣Ыn madopetam tv─Бm y─Бc─Бmahe

+Jamison Brereton

Most powerful Indra, your exhilaration that is conspicuous as the best drinker of soma,
with which you strike down the devourerтАФfor that we beg.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Although it is Indra whom we expect to be the best soma-drinker, here the epithet is transposed to his m├бda- тАШexhilarationтАЩ.

+Griffith

JOY, Mightiest Indra, known and marked, sprung most from Soma-draughts, wherewith

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Unlike Geldner I take sv├аrс╣Зara- here as an epithet of Adhrigu, rather than a PN (sim. VIII.3.12), though not on strong grounds, and VIII.6.39, where I do take it as a PN, undercuts this position.

Either Adhrigu or, if he is a personage, Svarс╣Зara receives the qualifier vep├бyant- тАШsetting atrembleтАЩ, without an object. Given how little we know about Adhrigu (or Svarс╣Зara), it is not clear what such an object might be, though it might refer to poetic inspiration.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAccepts, thunderer, their praise (offered) for the attainment of our desires, like consecrated butter;(induced) by which, you, promptly bear us by your might (to our objects).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

This praise song for dominance, purified like ghee, o master of the stones,
by which now in a single day with might you have waxed strongтАФ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner supplies a verb (verhilf) to govern the accusative phrase in ab, but given the parallelism of vss. 4 and 5, it is better that this phrase is governed by the juс╣гasva in 5a.

+Griffith

Accept this laud for aid, made pure like oil, thou Caster of the Stone,
Whereby even in a moment thou hast waxen great.

Diesem Lobgesang verhilf zur Geltung, der wie Schmalz abgekl├дrt ist, du Herr des Pre├Яsteins, durch den du sogleich an Kraft gewachsen bist.

+Grassmann

Dies Lob geniess zur Freude dir wie reines Schmalz, o Schleuderer, Durch das du alsobald mit Macht gewachsen bist.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(I glorify Indra) the deity, who, coming from afar, has given us, through friendship, (riches); heaping(them upon us) like rain from heaven, you have borne us (to our objects).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The god from afar who has become ready for partnership with usтАФ spreading like the one who spreads the rain from heaven [=Parjanya], you have waxed strong.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In c prath├бyan is used differently in simile and frame. In the former it is straightforwardly transitive, with vс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├нm as object; in the latter it is intransitive or, at least, absolute, as in, e.g., IV.53.2.

+Griffith

The God who from afar hath sent gifts to maintain our friendship’s bond,
Thou. spreading them like rain from heaven, hast waxen great.

+Geldner

Der Gott, der aus der Ferne zur Freundschaft f├╝r uns bereit ist, der du wie der den Regen des Himmels ausbreitende Parjanya gro├Я geworden bist.

+Grassmann

Der uns als Gott von ferne her gef├╝hrt hat zur Genossenschaft, Wie Himmelsdunst dich breitend bist gewachsen du.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe banners of Indra, the thunderbolt (he bears) in his hands, have brought (us benefits), when, likethe sun, he has expanded heaven and earth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

He has extended heaven and earth: i.e. when he has refreshedthem both with rain

+Jamison Brereton

His beacons waxed strong and the mace in his two hands,
when, like the sun, he made the two worlds grow.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the chaining between tс╣Ыcas, with the refrain of vss. 4-6 vav├бkс╣гitha, returning as the first word of the following verse, vavakс╣г├║с╕е, with person and number adjustment. Interestingly, it’s this verse where the Anhang refrain doesn’t precisely match the two following verses: ├бvardhayat versus pr├б v─Бvс╣Ыdhe, with the same root but different stem, and transitive versus intransitive. This is the only such deviation in this hymn.

+Griffith

The beams that mark him have grown strong, the thunder rests between his arms,
When, like the Sun, he hath increased both Heaven and Earth.

+Geldner

Seine Abzeichen und die Keule in seinen H├дnden sind gewachsen, als er wie die Sonne beide Welten gr├╢├Яer machte.

+Grassmann

Es wuchsen seine Lichter auf, und in den Armen ihm der Blitz, Als Erd’ und Himmel sonnengleich er kr├дftigte.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I take y├бdi in p─Бda a as standing for *y├бd ─л, with shortening before the cluster pr. See Jamison 2002. Hence тАШwhenтАЩ, not тАШifтАЩ. The *─л as usual functions as an accusative, anticipating the obj. sah├бsram mahiс╣г─Б╠Бn.

The word play between the voc. pravс╣Ыddha in a and the refrain verb pr├б v─Бvс╣Ыdhe cannot be easily captured in English.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, with the rays of the sun, utterly consumes his adversary; like fire (burning) the forests, hespreads victorious.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

With the rays of the sun Indra burns down Ar┼Ыas─Бna;
victorious like fire over the woods, he grew forth.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes the simile in c agn├нr v├бneva with ab: тАЬIndra brennt тАж den Ar┼Ыas─Бna nieder, wie Agni die B├дume,тАЭ with s─Бsah├нс╕е only construed with the refrain: тАЬder Siegreiche ist erstarktтАЭ (though see his n. on 9c). But this violates the structure of the rest of the hymn, where the c p─Бda hangs together. I therefore take the quality held in common between simile and frame to be s─Бsah├нс╕е. For тИЪsah with this simile see VIII.40.1 y├йn─Б dс╣Ыс╕╖h─Б╠БтАж s─Бhiс╣г─лmahi / agn├нr v├бneva… тАЬby which we might become victorious over the strongholds тАж as Agni (is victorious) over the woods,тАЭ and for the reduplicated -i-stem governing the accusative III.16.4 c├бkrir y├│ v├н┼Ыv─Б bh├║van─Бbh├н s─Бsah├нс╕е тАЬWho creates and overwhelms all living beingsтАжтАЭ On this nominal type and its syntactic behavior, see Grestenberger 2013 (JAOS 133).

Ar┼Ыas─Бna is an enemy of Indra in the RV about whom little is known.

VIII.12.10, 12: The verb initiating the refrain, m├нm─лte, is accented, and in these two verses the accent can be explained as a result of the status of the refrain; see above ad vss. 5-6. In 11 it starts a new clause and can owe its accent to that.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThis new praise, suited to the season, approaches, (Indra), to you; offering adoration and greatlydelighting (you), it verily proclaims the measure (of your merits).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Suited to the season: or, connected withsacrifice, с╣Ыtviy─Бvat─л; it verily proclaims the measure: mim─лta it: verily measures; indra gat─Бn guс╣З─Бnparicchinatti, it, the praise, discriminates the good properties attached to Indra, m─Бh─Бtmyam prakhy─Бpayati, itmakes known his greatness.

+Jamison Brereton

This newer visionary thought goes to you, conforming to her season [/to the ritual sequence].
Rendering service, dear to manyтАФshe is (well-)measured indeed.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Encouraged by the insistent feminines, с╣Ыtv├нy─Бyat─л here is a pun, referring both to ThoughtтАЩs conformity to the ritual order and to her menstrual cycle. See 80.7 for the same word play involving dh─л╠Бс╕е, where the femininity of the subject is more emphasized than here. It is possible that the refrain here тАЬshe is (well- )measured indeedтАЭ can also refer to the menstrual cycle. Otherwise it probably refers to the metrical character of the thought and perhaps the fact that she measures up even to IndraтАЩs great size. The refrain also has to be considered beside a phrase in the next hymn, VIII.13.30 m├нm─лte yaj├▒├бm ─Бnuс╣г├бk “measures the sacrifice in proper order.”

+Griffith

This newest thought of ours that suits the time approaches unto thee:
Serving, beloved in many a place it metes and marks.

+Geldner

F├╝r dich geht diese rechtzeitige Dichtung aufs neue hinaus, ehrerbietig, viellieb wird sie nach dem Versma├Я gemessen.

+Grassmann

Dies regelrechte Andachtslied, dies neue eilet hin zu dir, Anbetungsvoll und vielbeliebt, es ist bereit.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe devout praiser of the adorable (Indra) purifies in due succession the offering (of the Soma); withsacred hymns he magnifies (the might) of Indra; he verily proclaims the measure (of hismerits).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

As embryo of the sacrifice, seeking the gods, (the thought?) purifies its intention following the proper order.
By praises of Indra it has grownтАФit is (well-)measured indeed.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The subject of this verse is not made clear. Geldner suggests either st├│ma- or dh─лt├н-. The latter is more likely in my view, continued from vs. 10. There are no clashing non-feminines, since devay├║с╕е could serve either for masc. or fem., and in any case could be matching the gender of the g├бrbhaс╕е. Another possibility is Agni, since he is regularly called an embryo in these circumstances, but the unity of the tс╣Ыca speaks against this. I would therefore change the тАЬitтАЭs in the published translation (тАЬits intention,тАЭ тАЬit has grown,тАЭ тАЬit isтАЭ) to feminine forms, to match vs. 10.

The VP kr├бtum pun─лte of b is found in the next hymn, VIII.13.1b, where the subject is Indra, but that referent is not possible here.

+Griffith

The pious germ of sacrifice directly purifies the soul.
By Indra’s lauds it waxes great, it metes and marks.

+Geldner

Des Opfers neugeborenes Kind, das nach den G├╢ttern verlangt, l├дutert gr├╝ndlich seinen Geist. Durch Indra┬┤s Lobpreisungen ist es gro├Я geworden, es wird nach dem Versma├Я gemessen.

+Grassmann

Des Opfers gottgef├дll’ger Spross durchl├дutre stetig seine Kraft, Durch Indra’s Loblied ward er stark; er steht bereit.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, the benefactor of his friend (the worshipper), has enlarged himself to drik the Soma, in likemanner as the pious praise dilates and proclaims the measure (of his merits).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Proclaims the measure: like thedilating praise of the worshipper, it proclaims;

Pr─Бc─л = prakarс╣гeс╣Зa stutyam guс╣Зagaс╣Зam pr─Бpnuvat─л

+Jamison Brereton

Indra, who is the gain from our alliance, spreads himself out for soma-drinking.
(The thought) advancing like an axe for the presserтАФit is (well-) measured indeed.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Since s├бni- is only a nom. actionis, not an agent, it must mean тАШwinnings, gainтАЩ. What it must mean here is that Indra is what we win if we keep our part of the sacrificial bargain (mitr├б-).

The subject of c must again be the dh─лt├н-. So also Geldner But the point of the simile тАЬlike an axeтАЭ (v─Б╠Б┼Ы─лva) is somewhat unclear, though GeldnerтАЩs explanation seems reasonable: just as the thought is measured out metrically (m├нm─лta ├нd), so is an axe wielded in a regular rhythm (he compares VIII.19.23).

+Griffith

Indra who wins the friend hath spread himself to drink the Soma-draught:
Like worshipper’s dilating praise; it metes and marks.

+Geldner

Indra, der Gewinn der Freundschaft hat sich breit gemacht, um Soma zu trinken. -Sich im Takt vorw├дrts bewegend f├╝r den Somapresser wie eine Axt wird sie nach dem Versma├Я gemessen.

+Grassmann

Des Freundes Spende dehnt sich aus, so Indra auch zum Somatrunk, Gleich wie das Beil in Pressers Hand, ist sie bereit.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI pour the oblation of the sacrifice, like clarified butter, into the mouth (of that Indra), whom wise men,addressing with prayers, delight.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Whom [=Indra] the inspired ─Аyus, whose conveyance is solemn speech, have brought to exhilarationтАФ
like ghee, it swells in his mouthтАФ(the speech) that belongs to truth.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner interprets the verb abhipramand├║с╕е somewhat bizarrely as тАШgo on a pilgrimage toтАЩ (тАЬZu dem тАж die тАж ─АyuтАЩs тАж pilgertenтАЭ), presumably influenced by ukth├бv─Бhasaс╕е тАШwhose conveyance is solemn speechтАЩ. K├╝mmel (357) takes the same verb as intransitive, with the y├бm expressing the source of pleasure (тАЬAn dem die Erregten тАж sich (schon immer) erfreuenтАЭ). I see no reason why it is not a straight transitive тАЬbring to exhilarationтАЭ like other forms of the act. pf. of тИЪmad.

The question is what is the relationship between ab and c. Properly speaking, the y├бm should have a referent in the main clause (which is c: note the unaccented verb pipye), but there is no obvious candidate. Geldner simply treats ab as an unresolved relative clause, without comment. I assume that Indra, the presumed referent of y├бm in p─Бda a, is covertly present in c: it is his mouth in which the speech/hymn swells - the speech having been homologized to soma already by the тИЪmad form in b. See also 4ab where praise is compared to purified ghee, which may mediate the simile in our c, ghс╣Ыt├бm iva. Geldner, however, seems to take the mouth as belonging to the ─Аyus (тАЬтАж ihrem MundтАЭ); this would make sense as the source of the speech offered to Indra. Perhaps the lack of an overt genitive limiting тАШmouthтАЩ allows both interpretations some currency. I might therefore emend the published translation to тАЬit swells in his/their mouth.тАЭ

+Griffith

He whom the sages, living men, have gladdened, offering up their hymns,
Hath swelled like oil of sacrifice in Agni’s mouth.

+Geldner

Zu dem die redekundigen Ayu┬┤s im Fahrzeug der Lieder pilgerten, wie Schmalz quillt in ihrem Munde ├╝ber, was das Wort der Wahrheit ist.

+Grassmann

Ihm, den die muntre S├дngerschar durch Spr├╝che recht erheitert hat, Ihm schwillt wie Butter in dem Mund des Opfers Werk.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI glorify the divine Indra wherever worshipped for your protection; (my praises) have reached him for theprompt (fulfilment) of the (objects of the) sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Divine Indra: devam devam indram indram: i.e., Indra ispresent at the same time at different ceremonies, or in various forms; cf. RV. 6.047.18; the verse is addressed tothe priests and the yajam─Бna

+Jamison Brereton

Upon hymning the god time after time, for (him) to help you, upon hymning Indra time after time,
then they came through to victory for the sacrifice.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner tr. the infinitival gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣г├бni as a modal тАЬsoll тАж loben.тАЭ Similarly Keydana, who takes it as a тАЬmatrix infinitiveтАЭ with 2nd ps. subject but tr. modally (тАЬтАж sollt ihr euch zu Hilfe besingen,тАЭ 174, 246). Because it is locative in form, I am somewhat dubious about assigning it this value, which is typical, and understandable, for dative infinitivals.

I have reordered the elements in c to make the sentence parsable. That the refrain vy ─Б╠Аna┼Ыuс╕е should be construed with what precedes is shown by the parallel

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe thunderer, from whom neither the heaven and earth nor the firmament are separated; from thestrength of whom, the mighty one, (the world) derives lustre.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The mace-bearer whom the two worlds do not encompass, nor the midspaces,
just from his own onslaught he has flared upтАФentirely from his might.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the slight variation on the refrain: abl. ├│jasaс╕е, parallel to abl. ├бm─Бt in b, versus 22-23 dat. ├│jase.

Geldner supplies тАЬthe worldтАЭ (extracted from the dual of a) as subject of titviс╣гe in c.

I follow Oldenberg in taking Indra as subject, with the asya reflexive. As Oldenberg points out, in nearby VIII.6.5 it is IndraтАЩs ├│jas- that is subject of the same verb; here the attribute has been deflected to an oblique case and the god himself is subject. Note also X.55.1, where Indra is modified by the participle titviс╣г─Бn├бс╕е.

+Griffith

Not earth, nor heaven, nor firmaments contain the Thunder-wielding God:
They shake before his violent rush and vigorous strength.

+Geldner

Den weder die beiden Welten, noch die Luftr├дume fassen, den Keulentr├дger; vor seiner Wut geriet die Welt in Aufregung, vor seiner St├дrke.

+Grassmann

Den Erd’ und Himmel nicht umfasst, die L├╝fte nicht, den Blitzenden, Vor seinem Andrang bebt das All, und seiner Kraft.

+Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдГ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡реА рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛ рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░реЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рдЗрдорд╛рдВ рдкреБрд░реЛрд╡рд░реНрддрд┐рдиреАрдВ рдкрд┐рдкреНрд░рддреАрдВ рдкреВрдЬрдпрдиреНрддреАрдВ рдкреНрд░реАрдгрдпрдиреНрддреА рд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдЯреБрддрд┐рдВ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдВ рдзреАрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХрд░реНрдорднрд┐рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдЪрд░рдгреИрдГ рд╕рд╛рд░реНрдзрдВ рддреЗ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░ рдЗрдпрд░реНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЧрдордпрддрд┐ ред рдЬрд╛рдорд┐рдВ рдкрджреЗрд╡ рдпрдерд╛ рдмрдиреНрдзреБрднреВрддрдВ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдореБрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд┐ рдкрджрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe wise (worshipper), Indra, offers you this gratifying sincere praise along with pious rites at thesacrifice, as (a man plural ces) a kinsman in (a prominent) position.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The inspired poet, through his insights, raises this good praise to you, Indra, which guides its kin safely across, like footsteps, while the ceremony is pro(ceeding).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda c presents some difficulties of interpretation, in particular how to distribute the three accusatives j─Бm├нm, pad─Б╠Б, and p├нprat─лm. The last, a participle, takes pad├бm as object in IX.10.7 (adduced by both Oldenberg and Geldner): pad├бm ├йkasya p├нprataс╕е тАЬguiding the track of the lone one safely across.тАЭ But it also takes personal objects, as in nearby VIII.6.2 praj─Б╠Бm rt├бsya p ╠е ├нprataс╕е тАЬguiding the child of truth [=poem] safely across.тАЭ I therefore take it as a semantically mixed construction, with j─Бm├нm тАШkinтАЩ (which in this case, as in VIII.6.2, would be a poem or hymn) in the frame and тАШfootstepsтАЩ in the simile. By contrast, Geldner takes j─Бm├нm as the subject of the simile, parallel to suс╣гс╣нut├нm: тАЬdie wie eine Schwester deine Schritte geleitet.тАЭ His interpretation reads better, but ignores the position of iva and also the contrasting constructions of the participle p├нprat- elsewhere. By my interpretation the point is that the suс╣гс╣нut├н- produced in ab takes the rest of the verbal portion of the sacrifice along with it to the god.

I take the refrain pr─Б╠Бdhvar├й as a (quasi) locative absolute, as in VIII.46.18, rather than as integrated into what precedes.

+Griffith

To thee, O Indra, with this thought the sage lifts up this eulogy,
Akin and leading as on foot to sacrifice.

+Geldner

Diese Lobrede hebt der Redekundige f├╝r dich, Indra, gedankenvoll an, die wie eine Schwester deine Schritte geleitet, vorw├дrts zum Opfer;

+Grassmann

Dies Preislied bringt, o Indra, dir der S├дnger dar mit frommem Sinn, Das schwesterlich den Schritten folgt beim Opferfest.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen the congregated (worshippers) praise him aloud in a plural ce that plural ases (him) on the navel (of theearth), in the spot where the libation is effused at the sacrifice, (then).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Then: tad─Бn─лm dhanam pradehi:connects the verse with what follows– uttaratra sambandha; n─Бbh─Б yaj├▒asya dohan─Б pr─Бdhvare: the navelis the altar (pс╣Ыthivy─Б n─Бbhisth─Бn─лye);

Yaj├▒a = Soma;

Dohana = dohane abhiс╣гavasth─Бne

+Jamison Brereton

When they have sounded in unison in his own dear domain,
in the navel of the sacrifice, along with the milking, while the ceremony is pro(ceeding),

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Contrary to Geldner, I take p─Бda c as part of the subordinate clause of ab, with vs. 33 the main clause. Geldner is forced to supply a verb (тАЬgehtтАЭ).

doh├бn─Б is the problem here. Grassmann suggests we read it as underlying doh├бn─Бs as in I.144.2, despite the sandhi. This seems to be the basis of GeldnerтАЩs interpretation (тАЬdie MelkungтАЭ as subject), but Oldenberg rejects this and takes it as an instrumental. I weakly follow Oldenberg, but neither of the interpretations is particularly compelling.

+Griffith

When in thine own dear dwelling all gathered have lifted up the voice
Milk-streams at worship’s central spot, for sacrifice,

+Geldner

Wenn die S├дnger bei seiner lieben Erscheinung gemeinsam den Gesang angestimmt haben, dann geht im Nabel des Opfers die Melkung vor sich beim Opfer;

+Grassmann

Und wenn in deinem Lieblingssitz die Melker rauschen im Verein In der Verehrung Mittelpunkt beim Opferfest,

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬBestow upon us, Indra, (wealth), comprising worthy male ofspring, excellent horses, and good cattle;like the ministrant priest (I worship you) at the sacrifice, (to secure) your prior consideration.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Indra, give to us the possession of good heroes, of good horses, of good cows,
like a Hotar, (for us) to be first in your thought, while the ceremony is pro(ceeding).

+Griffith

As Priest, O Indra, give us wealth in brave men and good steeds ana kine
That we may first remember thee for sacrifice.

+Geldner

Gib uns, Indra, den Besitz guter Meister, guter Rosse, guter Rinder, damit wir zuerst bedacht werden, wie der Hotri beim Opfer!

+Grassmann

So gib uns, Indra, reiche Schar an S├╢hnen, Rossen, Rindern auch Auf ersten Wunsch als Priester du beim Opferfest.

+Elizarenkova
